            <small>Published on <time datetime="2012-09-13T14:57:49Z" itemprop="datePublished">Sep 13, 2012</time></small>

            <div class="slideshow-description-container add-padding-right">
              <div class="j-desc-more description"
                data-ga-cat="bigfoot_slideview"
                data-ga-action="description>more">

                <p class="notranslate">
                  Please email hall@coreservlets.com for info on how to arrange customized courses on Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2.2, PrimeFaces, Hadoop, jQuery&#x2F;Ajax, Android programming, and other Java EE topics onsite at

                    &hellip;
                    <a href="#"><i class="fa fa-caret-down"></i></a>
                </p>
              </div>

              <p class="j-desc-expand description description-expanded notranslate" itemprop="description">
                Please email hall@coreservlets.com for info on how to arrange customized courses on Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2.2, PrimeFaces, Hadoop, jQuery&#x2F;Ajax, Android programming, and other Java EE topics onsite at YOUR location.
<br />
<br />This is the second of two sections that cover OOP in Java. It discusses overloading, the use of private instance variables teamed with accessor (getter&#x2F;setter) methods, JavaDoc, and inheritance. It also very briefly summarizes some more advanced OOP concepts. See http:&#x2F;&#x2F;courses.coreservlets.com&#x2F;Course-Materials&#x2F;java.html for the full tutorial, associated code, exercises, and exercise solutions. You can also download PDF files of each lecture, for saving or printing. This lecture refers to changes in Java 8, but without much detail on Java 8 capabilities. Java 8 lambdas and streams are covered in a separate tutorial at http:&#x2F;&#x2F;www.coreservlets.com&#x2F;java-8-tutorial&#x2F; 
              </p>
            </div>

Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-5-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 5 image" target="_blank">
        5.
      </a>
    Overview
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Classes can have more than one method with the same
name, or more than one constructor.
&#x2013; The methods (or constructors) have to differ from each
other by having different number or types of arguments
&#x2022; Syntax
public class MyClass {
public double getRandomNum() { &#x2026;}; // Range 1-10
public double getRandomNum(double range) { &#x2026; }
}
&#x2022; Motivation
&#x2013; Methods: lets you have similar names for similar ops
&#x2013; Constructors: let you build instances in different ways
7
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-6-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 6 image" target="_blank">
        6.
      </a>
    Ship Example: Overloading
public class Ship4 { (In Ship4.java)
public double x=0.0, y=0.0, speed=1.0, direction=0.0;
public String name;
public Ship4(double x, double y,
double speed, double direction,
String name) {
this.x = x;
this.y = y;
this.speed = speed;
this.direction = direction;
this.name = name;
}
public Ship4(String name) {
this.name = name;
}
private double degreesToRadians(double degrees) {
return(degrees * Math.PI / 180.0);
}
...8
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-7-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 7 image" target="_blank">
        7.
      </a>
    Overloading (Continued)
...
public void move() {
move(1);
}
public void move(int steps) {
double angle = degreesToRadians(direction);
x = x + steps * speed * Math.cos(angle);
y = y + steps * speed * Math.sin(angle);
}
public void printLocation() {
System.out.println(name + " is at ("
+ x + "," + y + ").");
}
}9

public class Test4 { (In Test4.java)

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-9-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 9 image" target="_blank">
        9.
      </a>
    Overloading: Major Points
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Allows you to define more than one function or
constructor with the same name
&#x2022; Overloaded functions or constructors must differ in the
number or types of their arguments (or both), so that Java
can always tell which one you mean
&#x2022; Simple examples:
&#x2013; Here are two square methods that differ only in the
type of the argument; they would both be permitted inside
the same class definition.
// square(4) is 16
public int square(int x) { return(x*x); }
// square("four") is "four four"
public String square(String s) {
return(s + " " + s);
}11
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-10-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 10 image" target="_blank">
        10.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.
Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.
OOP Design:
Best Practices
12
Always code as if the guy who ends up maintaining your code
will be a violent psychopath who knows where you live.
&#x2013; John F. Woods
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-11-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 11 image" target="_blank">
        11.
      </a>
    Overview
&#x2022; Ideas
&#x2013; Instance variables should always be private
&#x2022; And hooked to outside world with getBlah and/or setBlah
&#x2013; From very beginning, put in JavaDoc-style comments
&#x2022; Syntax
/** Short summary. More detail. Can use HTML. */
public class MyClass {
private String firstName;
public String getFirstName() { return(firstName); }
public void setFirstName(String s) { firstName = s; }
}
&#x2022; Motivation
&#x2013; Limits ripple effect. Makes code more maintainable.
13
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-12-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 12 image" target="_blank">
        12.
      </a>
    Ship Example: OOP Design and
Usage
/** Ship example to demonstrate OOP in Java. */
public class Ship {
private double x=0.0, y=0.0, speed=1.0, direction=0.0;
private String name;
&#x2026;
/** Get current X location. */
public double getX() {
return(x);
}
/** Set current X location. */
public void setX(double x) {
this.x = x;
}
...14
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-13-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 13 image" target="_blank">
        13.
      </a>
    OOP Design: Testing and
Results
public class ShipTest { (In ShipTest.java)
public static void main(String[] args) {
Ship s1 = new Ship("Ship1");
Ship s2 = new Ship(0.0, 0.0, 2.0, 135.0, "Ship2");

Ship1 is at (1.0,0.0).
Ship2 is at (-4.24264...,4.24264...).15
You can also run JavaDoc from within Eclipse by starting at Project menu and choosing
&#x201C;Generate JavaDoc&#x201D;. If it asks you where javadoc.exe is located, you can find it in the bin
folder of your Java installation (e.g., C:Program FilesJavajdk1.7.0_45bin)

        15.
      </a>
    Major Points
&#x2022; Encapsulation
&#x2013; Lets you change internal representation and data
structures without users of your class changing their code
&#x2013; Lets you put constraints on values without users of your
class changing their code
&#x2013; Lets you perform arbitrary side effects without users of
your class changing their code
&#x2022; Comments and JavaDoc
&#x2013; Comments marked with /** ... */ will be part of the
online documentation
&#x2013; Call "javadoc *.java" to build online documentation.
&#x2013; See later slides for details

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-16-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 16 image" target="_blank">
        16.
      </a>
    More Details on Getters and
Setters
&#x2022; Eclipse will automatically build
getters/setters from instance variables
&#x2013; R-click anywhere in code
&#x2013; Choose Source &#xF0E0; Generate Getters and Setters
&#x2013; However, if you later click on instance variable and do
Refactor &#xF0E0; Rename, Eclipse will not automatically
rename the accessor methods

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-17-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 17 image" target="_blank">
        17.
      </a>
    More Details on Getters and
Setters
&#x2022; There need not be both getters and setters
&#x2013; It is common to have fields that can be set at instantiation,
but never changed again (immutable field). It is even
quite common to have classes containing only immutable
fields (immutable classes)
public class Ship {
private final String shipName;
public Ship(&#x2026;) { shipName = &#x2026;; &#x2026; }
public String getName() { return(shipName); }
// No setName method
}19
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-18-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 18 image" target="_blank">
        18.
      </a>
    More Details on Getters and
Setters
&#x2022; Getter/setter names need not correspond to
instance variable names
&#x2013; Common to do so if there is a simple correspondence, but
this is not required
&#x2022; Notice on previous page that instance var was
&#x201C;shipName&#x201D;, but methods were &#x201C;getName&#x201D; and &#x201C;setName&#x201D;
&#x2013; In fact, there doesn&#x2019;t even have to be a corresponding
instance variable
public class Customer {
&#x2026;
public String getFirstName() { getFromDatabase(&#x2026;); }
public void setFirstName(&#x2026;) { storeInDatabase(&#x2026;); }
public double getBonus() { return(Math.random()); }
}

Inheritance
21
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-20-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 20 image" target="_blank">
        20.
      </a>
    Overview
&#x2022; Ideas
&#x2013; You can make a class that &#x201C;inherits&#x201D; characteristics of
another class
&#x2022; The original class is called &#x201C;parent class&#x201D;, &#x201C;super class&#x201D;, or
&#x201C;base class&#x201D;. The new class is called &#x201C;child class&#x201D;,
&#x201C;subclass&#x201D;, or &#x201C;extended class&#x201D;.
&#x2013; The child class has access to all non-private methods of
the parent class.
&#x2022; No special syntax need to call inherited methods
&#x2022; Syntax
&#x2013; public class ChildClass extends ParentClass { &#x2026; }
&#x2022; Motivation
&#x2013; Supports the key OOP idea of code reuse (i.e., don&#x2019;t write
the same code twice). Design class hierarchies so that
shared behavior is inherited to all classes that need it.
22
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-21-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 21 image" target="_blank">
        21.
      </a>
    Simple Example
&#x2022; Person
public class Person {
public String getFirstName() { &#x2026; }
public String getLastName() { &#x2026; }
}
&#x2022; Employee
public class Employee extends Person {
public double getSalary() { &#x2026; }
public String getEmployeeInfo() {
return(getFirstName() + " " + getLastName() +
" earns " + getSalary());
}
}

      </a>

private String color = "red";

super(name);
setSpeed(20);
}
public Speedboat(double x, double y,
double speed, double direction,

super(x, y, speed, direction, name);
setColor(color);
}
@Override // Optional -- discussed later
public void printLocation() {
System.out.print(getColor().toUpperCase() + " ");
super.printLocation();
}
...
}24

public class SpeedboatTest {
public static void main(String[] args) {
Speedboat s1 = new Speedboat("Speedboat1");
Speedboat s2 = new Speedboat(0.0, 0.0, 2.0, 135.0,
"Speedboat2", "blue");

s1.move();
s2.move();

s2.printLocation();
s3.printLocation();

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-25-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 25 image" target="_blank">
        25.
      </a>
    Ship Inheritance Example:
Major Points
&#x2022; Format for defining subclasses
&#x2022; Using inherited methods
&#x2022; Using super(&#x2026;) for inherited constructors
&#x2013; Only when the zero-arg constructor is not OK
&#x2022; The most common case is to omit super and use zero-arg
constructor of parent, but super is used moderately often
&#x2022; Using super.someMethod(&#x2026;) for inherited
methods
&#x2013; Only when there is a name conflict
&#x2022; Used very rarely
27
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-26-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 26 image" target="_blank">
        26.
      </a>
    Inheritance
&#x2022; Syntax for defining subclasses
public class NewClass extends OldClass {
...
}
&#x2022; Nomenclature:
&#x2013; The old class is called the superclass, base class or parent class
&#x2013; The new class is called the subclass, derived class or child class
&#x2022; Effect of inheritance
&#x2013; Subclasses automatically have all public fields and methods of the
parent class
&#x2013; You don&#x2019;t need any special syntax to access the inherited fields and
methods; you use the exact same syntax as with locally defined
fields or methods.
&#x2013; You can also add in fields or methods not available in the superclass
&#x2022; Java doesn&#x2019;t support multiple inheritance
&#x2013; A class can only have one direct parent. But grandparent and great-
grandparent (etc.) are legal and common.
28
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-27-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 27 image" target="_blank">
        27.
      </a>
    Inherited constructors and
super(...)
&#x2022; Zero-arg constructor of parent called
&#x2013; When you instantiate an object of a subclass, the system will
always call the superclass constructor first
&#x2022; By default, the zero-argument superclass constructor is called
&#x2022; If you want to specify that a different parent constructor is called,
invoke the parent class constructor with super(args)
&#x2022; If super(&#x2026;) is used in a subclass constructor, then super(&#x2026;) must
be the first statement in the constructor
&#x2022; Constructor life-cycle
&#x2013; Each constructor has three phases:
1. Invoke the constructor of the superclass
&#x2022; The zero-argument constructor is called automatically. No special syntax
is needed unless you want a different parent constructor.
2. Initialize all instance variables based on their initialization
statements
3. Execute the body of the constructor
29
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-28-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 28 image" target="_blank">
        28.
      </a>
    Overridden methods and
super.methodName(...)
&#x2022; Idea of overriding
&#x2013; When a class defines a method using the same name,
return type, and arguments as a method in the superclass,
then the class overrides the method in the superclass
&#x2013; Only non-static methods can be overridden
&#x2022; Distinguishing between local and inherited
methods (rare!)
&#x2013; If there is a locally defined method and an inherited
method that have the same name and take the same
arguments, you can use the following to refer to the
inherited method
&#x2022; super.methodName(...)
&#x2022; super.super.methodName is illegal
30
 
  </li>

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-29-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 29 image" target="_blank">
        29.

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-39-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 39 image" target="_blank">
        39.
      </a>
    Abstract Classes
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; A class that you cannot directly instantiate (i.e., on which
you cannot use &#x201C;new&#x201D;). But you can subclass it and
instantiate the subclasses.
&#x2022; Syntax
public abstract class SomeClass {
public abstract SomeType method1(&#x2026;); // No body
public SomeType method2(&#x2026;) { &#x2026; } // Not abstract
}
&#x2022; Motivation
&#x2013; Guarantees that all subclasses will have certain methods
&#x2013; Lets you make collections of mixed types
41
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-40-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 40 image" target="_blank">
        40.
      </a>
    Abstract Classes: Problem
&#x2022; You have
&#x2013; Circle and Rectangle classes, each with getArea methods
&#x2022; Goal
&#x2013; Get sum of areas of an array of Circles and Rectangles
&#x2022; Why does this fail?
Object[] shapes =
{ new Circle(&#x2026;), new Rectangle(&#x2026;) &#x2026; };
double sum = 0;
for(Object shape: shapes) {
sum = sum + shape.getArea();
}
42
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-41-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 41 image" target="_blank">
        41.
      </a>
    Abstract Classes: Solution
&#x2022; Shape
public abstract class Shape {
public abstract double getArea();
public void printInfo() {
System.out.println(getClass().getSimpleName() +
" has area " + getArea());
}
}
&#x2022; Circle (and similar for Rectangle)
public class Circle extends Shape {
public double getArea() { &#x2026; }
}
43
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-42-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 42 image" target="_blank">
        42.
      </a>
    Interfaces
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; A model for a class. More or less an abstract class but without
any concrete methods.
&#x2022; However, Java 8 interfaces can have concrete (default) methods
&#x2022; Syntax
public interface SomeInterface {
public SomeType method1(&#x2026;); // No body
public SomeType method2(&#x2026;); // No body
}
public class SomeClass implements SomeInterface {
// Real definitions of method1 and method 2
}
&#x2022; Motivation
&#x2013; Like abstract classes, guarantees classes have certain methods.
But classes can implement multiple interfaces.44
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-43-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 43 image" target="_blank">
        43.
      </a>
    Interfaces: Problem
&#x2022; Sum of areas
&#x2013; You again want to get sum of areas of mixture of Circles
and Rectangles.
&#x2022; But, this time you do not need Shape &#x201C;class&#x201D; to have a
concrete printInfo method
&#x2022; Why interface instead of abstract class?
&#x2013; Classes can directly extend only one class (abstract or
otherwise)
&#x2013; Classes can implement many interfaces
public class Foo extends Bar implements Baz, Boo {
&#x2026;
}
45
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-44-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 44 image" target="_blank">
        44.
      </a>
    Interfaces: Solution
&#x2022; Shape
public interface Shape {
public double getArea();
}
&#x2022; Circle
public class Circle implements Shape {
public double getArea(&#x2026;) { &#x2026; }
}
&#x2022; Rectangle
public class Rectangle implements Shape {
public double getArea() { &#x2026; }
}
46
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-45-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 45 image" target="_blank">
        45.
      </a>
    Java 8: Interfaces
and Abstract Classes
47
Java 7 and Earlier Java 8
Abstract
Classes
&#x2022; Can have concrete methods and
abstract methods
&#x2022; Can have static methods
&#x2022; Can have instance variables
&#x2022; Class can directly extend one
(Same as Java 7)
Interfaces &#x2022; Can only have abstract methods
&#x2013; no concrete methods
&#x2022; Cannot have static methods
&#x2022; Cannot have instance variables
&#x2022; Class can implement any
number
&#x2022; Can have concrete (default)
methods and abstract
methods
&#x2022; Can have static methods
&#x2022; Cannot have instance
variables
&#x2022; Class can implement any
number
Conclusion: there is little reason to use abstract classes in Java 8. Except for
instance variables, Java 8 interfaces can do everything that abstract classes can
do, plus are more flexible since classes can implement more than one interface.
This means that Java 8 has real multiple inheritance.
public interface Blah {
default String someMessage() {&#x2026;}
&#x2026;
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-46-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 46 image" target="_blank">
        46.
      </a>
    Using @Override
&#x2022; Parent class
public class Ellipse implements Shape {
public double getArea() { &#x2026; }
}
&#x2022; Child class (mistake!)
public class Circle extends Ellipse {
public double getarea() { &#x2026; }
}
&#x2022; Catching mistake at compile time
public class Circle extends Ellipse {
@Override
public double getarea() { &#x2026; }
}48
This code will compile, but when you call
getArea at runtime, you will get version from
Ellipse, since there was a typo in this name
(lowercase a).
If Ellipse does not properly define getArea, code won&#x2019;t
even compile since then the class does not satisfy the
requirements of the interface.
This tells the compiler &#x201C;I think that I am
overriding a method from the parent class&#x201D;. If
there is no such method in the parent class,
code won&#x2019;t compile. If there is such a method
in the parent class, then @Override has no
effect on the code. Recommended but optional.
More on @Override in later sections.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-47-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 47 image" target="_blank">
        47.
      </a>
    CLASSPATH
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; The CLASSPATH environment variable defines a list of
directories in which to look for classes
&#x2022; Default = current directory and system libraries
&#x2022; Best practice is to not set this when first learning Java!
&#x2022; Setting the CLASSPATH
set CLASSPATH = .;C:java;D:cwpechoserver.jar
setenv CLASSPATH .:~/java:/home/cwp/classes/
&#x2013; The &#x201C;.&#x201D; indicates the current working directory
&#x2022; Supplying a CLASSPATH
javac &#x2013;classpath .;D:cwp WebClient.java
java &#x2013;classpath .;D:cwp WebClient
49
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-48-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 48 image" target="_blank">
        48.
      </a>
    Packages
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Organize classes in groups.
&#x2022; Syntax
&#x2013; To put your code in package
&#x2022; Make folder called &#x201C;somepackage&#x201D; (in Eclipse, R-click on &#x201C;src&#x201D;
and do New &#xF0E0; Package)
&#x2022; put &#x201C;package somepackage&#x201D; at top of file (automatic in Eclipse)
&#x2013; To use code from another package
&#x2022; put &#x201C;import somepackage.*&#x201D; in file below your package
statement
&#x2022; Motivation
&#x2013; You only have to worry about name conflicts within your
package.
&#x2022; So, team members can work on different parts of project without
worrying about what class names the other teams use.50
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-49-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 49 image" target="_blank">
        49.
      </a>
    Visibility Modifiers
&#x2022; public
&#x2013; This modifier indicates that the variable or method can be
accessed anywhere an instance of the class is accessible
&#x2013; A class may also be designated public, which means
that any other class can use the class definition
&#x2013; The name of a public class must match the filename, thus
a file can have only one public class
&#x2022; private
&#x2013; A private variable or method is only accessible from
methods within the same class
&#x2013; Declare all instance variables private
&#x2013; Declare methods private if they are not part of class
contract and are just internal implementation helpers
51
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-50-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 50 image" target="_blank">
        50.
      </a>
    Visibility Modifiers (Continued)
&#x2022; protected
&#x2013; Protected variables or methods can only be accessed by
methods within the class, within classes in the same
package, and within subclasses
&#x2022; [default]
&#x2013; Default visibility indicates that the variable or method can
be accessed by methods within the class, and within
classes in the same package
&#x2013; A variable or method has default visibility if a modifier is
omitted . Rarely used!
&#x2022; private: very common. Use this as first choice.
&#x2022; public: common for methods and constructors. 2nd choice
&#x2022; protected: usually for instance vars only. Moderately rare.
&#x2022; default: very rare. Don&#x2019;t omit modifier without good reason.52
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-51-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 51 image" target="_blank">
        51.
      </a>
    Visibility Summary
53
Modifiers
Data Fields and Methods public protected default private
Accessible from same class? yes yes yes yes
Accessible to classes (nonsubclass) yes yes yes no
from the same package?
Accessible to subclass from the yes yes yes no
same package?
Accessible to classes (nonsubclass) yes no no no
from different package?
Accessible to subclasses from yes no no no
different package?
Inherited by subclass in the yes yes yes no
same package?
Inherited by subclass in different yes yes no no
package?
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-52-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 52 image" target="_blank">
        52.
      </a>
    Other Modifiers
&#x2022; final
&#x2013; For a variable: cannot be changed after instantiation
&#x2022; Widely used to make &#x201C;immutable&#x201D; classes
&#x2013; For a class: cannot be subclassed
&#x2013; For a method: cannot be overridden in subclasses
&#x2022; synchronized
&#x2013; Sets a lock on a section of code or method
&#x2022; Only one thread can access the code at any given time
&#x2022; volatile
&#x2013; Guarantees other threads see changes to variable
&#x2022; transient
&#x2013; Variables are not stored in serialized objects
&#x2022; native
&#x2013; Indicates that the method is implement using C or C++54
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-53-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 53 image" target="_blank">
        53.
      </a>
    Comments and JavaDoc
&#x2022; Java supports 3 types of comments
&#x2013; // Comment to end of line.
&#x2013; /* Block comment containing multiple lines.
Nesting of comments in not permitted. */
&#x2013; /** A JavaDoc comment placed before class
definition and nonprivate methods.
Text may contain (most) HTML tags,
hyperlinks, and JavaDoc tags. */
&#x2022; JavaDoc
&#x2013; Used to generate on-line documentation
javadoc Foo.java Bar.java (or *.java)
&#x2013; JavaDoc Home Page
&#x2022; http://java.sun.com/javase/6/docs/technotes/tools/windows/javadoc.html
55
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-54-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 54 image" target="_blank">
        54.
      </a>
    Useful JavaDoc Tags
&#x2022; @author
&#x2013; Specifies the author of the document
&#x2013; Must use javadoc &#x2013;author ... to generate in output
/** Description of some class ...
*
* @author &lt;A HREF="mailto:hall@coreservlets.com"&gt;
* Marty Hall&lt;/A&gt;
*/
&#x2022; @version
&#x2013; Version number of the document
&#x2013; Must use javadoc &#x2013;version ... to generate in output
&#x2022; @param
&#x2013; Documents a method argument
&#x2022; @return
&#x2013; Documents the return type of a method
56
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-55-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 55 image" target="_blank">
        55.
      </a>
    Useful JavaDoc Command-line
Arguments
&#x2022; -author
&#x2013; Includes author information (omitted by default)
&#x2022; -version
&#x2013; Includes version number (omitted by default)
&#x2022; -noindex
&#x2013; Tells javadoc not to generate a complete index
&#x2022; -notree
&#x2013; Tells javadoc not to generate the tree.html class hierarchy
&#x2022; -link, -linkoffline
&#x2013; Tells javadoc where to look to resolve links to other packages
-link http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.5.0/docs/api/
-linkoffline http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.5.0/docs/api/
c:jdk1.5docsapi
57
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-56-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 56 image" target="_blank">
        56.
      </a>
    JavaDoc: Example
/** Ship example to demonstrate OOP in Java.
*
* @author &lt;a href="mailto:hall@coreservlets.com"&gt;
* Marty Hall&lt;/a&gt;
*/
public class Ship {
private double x=0.0, y=0.0, speed=1.0, direction=0.0;
private String name;
/** Build a ship with specified parameters. */
public Ship(double x, double y, double speed,
double direction, String name) {
setX(x);
setY(y);
setSpeed(speed);
setDirection(direction);
setName(name);
}
...
58
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-57-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 57 image" target="_blank">
        57.

    JavaDoc: Example
&gt; javadoc -link http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.5.0/docs/api/
-author *.java
59
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-58-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 58 image" target="_blank">
        58.
      </a>
    The toString Method
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; If you give a class a toString method, that method is
automatically called whenever
&#x2022; An object of that class is converted to a String
&#x2022; An object of that class is printed
&#x2022; Example
public class Person {
// Main code covered earlier
@Override
public String toString() {
return("PERSON: " + getFullName());
}
}
60
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-59-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 59 image" target="_blank">
        59.
      </a>
    Enums
&#x2022; Java enums are classes with named
instances
&#x2013; They do not correspond to ints as in C++
&#x2022; Quick example
&#x2013; public enum Month { JANUARY, &#x2026;, DECEMBER }
&#x2013; doSomethingWith(Month.JANUARY);
&#x2022; Capabilities
&#x2013; Enums can have methods and constructors, just like
normal classes. Can be referenced in switch statements.
&#x2022; More info and examples
&#x2013; http://docs.oracle.com/javase/tutorial/java/javaOO/enum.html
61
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-60-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 60 image" target="_blank">
        60.
      </a>

Wrap-Up

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-61-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 61 image" target="_blank">
        61.
      </a>
    Java OOP References
&#x2022; Online
&#x2013; &#x201C;OOP Concepts&#x201D; section in Oracle Java Tutorial. See also &#x201C;Classes
and Objects&#x201D; and &#x201C;Interfaces and Inheritance&#x201D;.
&#x2022; http://docs.oracle.com/javase/tutorial/java/
&#x2022; Books
&#x2013; Murach&#x2019;s Java SE (Murach, Steelman, and Lowe)
&#x2022; Excellent Java intro for beginners to Java (but not first-time
programmers). Very good OOP section.
&#x2013; Thinking in Java (Bruce Eckel)
&#x2022; Perhaps not quite as good as Murach&#x2019;s book in general, but
possibly the best OOP coverage of any Java programming book.
&#x2013; Effective Java, 2nd Edition (Josh Bloch)
&#x2022; In my opinion, by far the best Java best-practices book ever written.
Fantastic coverage of OOP best practices.
&#x2013; However, very advanced. Other than the OOP chapter, you won&#x2019;t understand
much unless you have been doing Java fulltime for at least a year.
&#x2013; Even experts will learn a lot from this book.
63
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-62-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 62 image" target="_blank">
        62.
      </a>
    Summary
&#x2022; Overloading
&#x2013; You can have multiple methods or constructors with the
same name. They must differ in argument signatures
(number and/or type of arguments).
&#x2022; Best practices
&#x2013; Make all instance variables private
&#x2013; Hook them to the outside with getBlah and/or setBlah
&#x2013; Use JavaDoc-style comments from the very beginning
&#x2022; Inheritance
&#x2013; public class Subclass extends Superclass { &#x2026; }
&#x2022; Non-private methods available with no special syntax
&#x2022; Use super() on first line of constructor if you need non-
default parent constructor (moderately common)
&#x2022; Use super.method(&#x2026;) if local method and inherited
method have the same name (rare!)64
 
  </li>

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/05-java-oop-more-120913145751-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-objectoriented-programming-oop-in-java-more-capabilities-63-638.jpg?cb=1425321969" title="View slide 63 image" target="_blank">
        63.
      </a>

        });


      // Load more atb when clicked
      $('.j-lazy-thumb-click').lazyload({
        event : 'more-tab-clicked'
      });

      $('.j-more-tab').on('click', function() {
        $('.j-lazy-thumb-click').trigger('more-tab-clicked');
      });

      // Load additionnal css
      $(window).load(function() {
        loadCSS("//public.slidesharecdn.com/b/ss_foundation/stylesheets/slideview.css?cb2affaf5bbe25a22f663a9dc7e2048596a54fcc");
      });
    });
  </script>

    <img height="1" width="1" alt="" style="display:none;"
      src="//www.bizographics.com/collect/?pid=870&fmt=gif" />
  </noscript>

  </body>
